CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Standard deviation</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">dispersion of the values of a random variable around its expected value</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Standard_deviation_(disambiguation)" title="Standard deviation (disambiguation)">Standard deviation (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Standard_deviation_diagram.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/220px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/330px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/440px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Standard_deviation_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A plot of <a href="/wiki/Normal_distribution" title="Normal distribution">normal distribution</a> (or bell-shaped curve) where each band has a width of 1 standard deviation&#160;&#8211; See also: <a href="/wiki/68%E2%80%9395%E2%80%9399.7_rule" title="68&#8211;95&#8211;99.7 rule">68&#8211;95&#8211;99.7 rule</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="899" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg/220px-Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg/330px-Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg/440px-Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Normal-distribution-cumulative-density-function.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cumulative probability of a normal distribution with expected value 0 and standard deviation 1.</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistics</a>, the <b>standard deviation</b> (<b>SD</b>, also represented by the lower case Greek letter sigma <b><a href="/wiki/Sigma" title="Sigma">&#963;</a></b> or the Latin letter <a href="/wiki/S" title="S">s</a>) is a measure that is used to quantify the amount of variation or <a href="/wiki/Statistical_dispersion" title="Statistical dispersion">dispersion</a> of a set of data values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StatNotes_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-StatNotes-1">[1]</a></sup> A low standard deviation indicates that the data points tend to be close to the <a href="/wiki/Mean" title="Mean">mean</a> (also called the expected value) of the set, while a high standard deviation indicates that the data points are spread out over a wider range of values.\n</p><p>The standard deviation of a <a href="/wiki/Random_variable" title="Random variable">random variable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statistical_population" title="Statistical population">statistical population</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_set" title="Data set">data set</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Probability_distribution" title="Probability distribution">probability distribution</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">square root</a> of its <a href="/wiki/Variance" title="Variance">variance</a>.  It is <a href="/wiki/Algebra" title="Algebra">algebraically</a> simpler, though in practice less <a href="/wiki/Robust_statistics" title="Robust statistics">robust</a>, than the <a href="/wiki/Average_absolute_deviation" title="Average absolute deviation">average absolute deviation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>\nA useful property of the standard deviation is that, unlike the variance, it is expressed in the same units as the data. \n</p><p>In addition to expressing the variability of a population, the standard deviation is commonly used to measure confidence in statistical conclusions.  For example, the <a href="/wiki/Margin_of_error" title="Margin of error">margin of error</a> in <a href="/wiki/Opinion_poll" title="Opinion poll">polling</a> data is determined by calculating the expected standard deviation in the results if the same poll were to be conducted multiple times.  This derivation of a standard deviation is often called the "<a href="/wiki/Standard_error" title="Standard error">standard error</a>" of the estimate or "standard error of the mean" when referring to a mean.  It is computed as the standard deviation of all the means that would be computed from that population if an infinite number of samples were drawn and a mean for each sample were computed.\n</p><p>It is very important to note that the standard deviation of a population and the standard error of a statistic derived from that population (such as the mean) are quite different but related (related by the inverse of the square root of the number of observations). The reported margin of error of a poll is computed from the standard error of the mean (or alternatively from the product of the standard deviation of the population and the inverse of the square root of the sample size, which is the same thing) and is typically about twice the standard deviation&#8212;the half-width of a 95 percent <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval" title="Confidence interval">confidence interval</a>.  \n</p><p>In science, many researchers report the standard deviation of experimental data, and only effects that fall much farther than two standard deviations away from what would have been expected are considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statistically_significant" title="Statistically significant">statistically significant</a>&#8212;normal random error or variation in the measurements is in this way distinguished from likely genuine effects or associations.  The standard deviation is also important in finance, where the standard deviation on the <a href="/wiki/Rate_of_return" title="Rate of return">rate of return</a> on an investment is a measure of the <a href="/wiki/Volatility_(finance)" title="Volatility (finance)">volatility</a> of the investment.\n</p><p>When only a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statistical_sample" title="Statistical sample">sample</a> of data from a population is available, the term <b>standard deviation of the sample</b> or <b>sample standard deviation</b> can refer to either the above-mentioned quantity as applied to those data or to a modified quantity that is an unbiased estimate of the <b>population standard deviation</b> (the standard deviation of the entire population).\n</p>\n<div class="toc" title="Edit section: Basic examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_standard_deviation_of_metabolic_rate_of_northern_fulmars">Sample standard deviation of metabolic rate of northern fulmars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Sample standard deviation of metabolic rate of northern fulmars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Logan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Logan2010_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Logan2010-4">[4]</a></sup>\ngives the following example. Furness and Bryant<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FurnessBryant1996_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FurnessBryant1996-5">[5]</a></sup> measured the resting <a href="/wiki/Basal_metabolic_rate" title="Basal metabolic rate">metabolic rate</a> for 8 male and 6 female breeding <a href="/wiki/Northern_fulmar" title="Northern fulmar">northern fulmars</a>. The table shows the Furness data set.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Furness data set on metabolic rates of northern fulmars\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Sex</th>\n<th>Metabolic rate</th>\n<th>Sex</th>\n<th>Metabolic rate\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>525.8</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>727.7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>605.7</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1086.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>843.3</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1091.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>1195.5</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1361.3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>1945.6</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1490.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>2135.6</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1956.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>2308.7</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Male</td>\n<td>2950.0</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The graph shows the metabolic rate for males and females. By visual inspection, it appears that the variability of the metabolic rate is greater for males than for females.\n</p><p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg" title="Graph of metabolic rates for northern fulmars"><img alt="Graph of metabolic rates for northern fulmars" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="570" decoding="async" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg/570px-Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg/855px-Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg/1140px-Metabolic_rates_for_northern_fulmars.svg.png 2x" width="570"/></a>\n</p><p>The sample standard deviation of the metabolic rate for the female fulmars is calculated as follows. The formula for the sample standard deviation is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9f2b2061a0bda785c7d246d21ec20a17c79185e0" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:22.513ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where \n<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mo>&#8230;<!-- &#8230; --></mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c14e1c22ce19d99df6409a800191a33818ad3229" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.487ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> are the observed values of the sample items, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3199cb53071b8a4c7d5652988e10b5135e2fb638" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the mean value of these observations, and\n<i>N</i> is the number of observations in the sample.\n</p><p>In the sample standard deviation formula, for this example, the numerator is the sum of the squared deviation of each individual animal\'s metabolic rate from the mean metabolic rate. The table below shows the calculation of this sum of squared deviations for the female fulmars. For females, the sum of squared deviations is 886047.09, as shown in the table.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Sum of squares calculation for female fulmars\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Animal</th>\n<th>Sex</th>\n<th>Metabolic rate</th>\n<th>Mean</th>\n<th>Difference from mean</th>\n<th>Squared difference from mean\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>727.7</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>-557.8</td>\n<td>311140.84\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1086.5</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>-199.0</td>\n<td>39601.00\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1091.0</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>-194.5</td>\n<td>37830.25\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>4</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1361.3</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>75.8</td>\n<td>5745.64\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1490.5</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>205.0</td>\n<td>42025.00\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6</td>\n<td>Female</td>\n<td>1956.1</td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td>670.6</td>\n<td>449704.36\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="6">\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3"><i>Mean of metabolic rates</i></td>\n<td>1285.5</td>\n<td><i>Sum of squared differences</i></td>\n<td>886047.09\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The denominator in the sample standard deviation formula is <i>N</i> &#8211; 1, where <i>N</i> is the number of animals. In this example, there are <i>N</i> = 6 females, so the denominator is 6 &#8211; 1 = 5. The sample standard deviation for the female fulmars is therefore\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}={\\sqrt {\\frac {886047.09}{5}}}=420.96.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mn>886047.09</mn>\n<mn>5</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>420.96.</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}={\\sqrt {\\frac {886047.09}{5}}}=420.96.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {\\frac {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}{N-1}}}={\\sqrt {\\frac {886047.09}{5}}}=420.96.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dec45ed7195dae589a3c4b48d80fd8089674fe5c" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:48.275ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>For the male fulmars, a similar calculation gives a sample standard deviation of 894.37, approximately twice as large as the standard deviation for the females. The graph shows the metabolic rate data, the means (red dots), and the standard deviations (red lines) for females and males.\n</p><p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg" title="Graph of standard deviation of metabolic rate of fulmars"><img alt="Graph of standard deviation of metabolic rate of fulmars" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="534" decoding="async" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg/534px-SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg/801px-SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg/1068px-SD_of_metabolic_rate_of_fulmars.svg.png 2x" width="534"/></a>\n</p><p>Use of the sample standard deviation implies that these 14 fulmars are a sample from a larger population of fulmars. If these 14 fulmars comprised the entire population (perhaps the last 14 surviving fulmars), then instead of the sample standard deviation, the calculation would use the population standard deviation. In the population standard deviation formula, the denominator is <i>N</i> instead of <i>N</i> - 1. It is rare that measurements can be taken for an entire population, so, by default, statistical <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">computer programs</a> calculate the sample standard deviation. Similarly, journal articles report the sample standard deviation unless otherwise specified.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_standard_deviation_of_grades_of_eight_students">Population standard deviation of grades of eight students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Population standard deviation of grades of eight students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Suppose that the entire population of interest was eight students in a particular class. For a finite set of numbers, the population standard deviation is found by taking the <a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">square root</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arithmetic_average" title="Arithmetic average">average</a> of the squared deviations of the values subtracted from their average value. The marks of a class of eight students (that is, a <a href="/wiki/Statistical_population" title="Statistical population">statistical population</a>) are the following eight values:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 2,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 5,\\ 5,\\ 7,\\ 9.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>7</mn>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mn>9.</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 2,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 5,\\ 5,\\ 7,\\ 9.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="2,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 4,\\ 5,\\ 5,\\ 7,\\ 9." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e7c0d44f87d7dcc46301efa28031639498d4313e" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.249ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>These eight data points have the mean (average) of 5:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu ={\\frac {2+4+4+4+5+5+7+9}{8}}=5.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>7</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>9</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mn>8</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>5.</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu ={\\frac {2+4+4+4+5+5+7+9}{8}}=5.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mu ={\\frac {2+4+4+4+5+5+7+9}{8}}=5.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef618a62ad5547deb0f744b4df268a2ff4e15eee" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:39.426ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>First, calculate the deviations of each data point from the mean, and <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">square</a> the result of each:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\begin{array}{lll}(2-5)^{2}=(-3)^{2}=9&amp;&amp;(5-5)^{2}=0^{2}=0\\\\(4-5)^{2}=(-1)^{2}=1&amp;&amp;(5-5)^{2}=0^{2}=0\\\\(4-5)^{2}=(-1)^{2}=1&amp;&amp;(7-5)^{2}=2^{2}=4\\\\(4-5)^{2}=(-1)^{2}=1&amp;&amp;(9-5)^{2}=4^{2}=16.\\\\\\end{array}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtable columnalign="left left left" columnspacing="1em" rowspacing="4pt">\n<mtr>\n<mtd>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n<mtr>\n<mtd>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mtd>\n<mtd></mtd>\n<mtd>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>5</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mtd>\n<mtd></mtd>\n<mtd>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>9</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; margin-top: -0.331ex; width:46.033ex; height:13.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Variance" title="Variance">variance</a> is the mean of these values:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ^{2}={\\frac {9+1+1+1+0+0+4+16}{8}}=4.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>9</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>16</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mn>8</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>4.</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma ^{2}={\\frac {9+1+1+1+0+0+4+16}{8}}=4.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ^{2}={\\frac {9+1+1+1+0+0+4+16}{8}}=4.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/93c1d982a0d72a8b35a6a52700a7118d3cbd7429" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:41.572ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>and the <i>population</i> standard deviation is equal to the square root of the variance:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {4}}=2.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mn>4</mn>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2.</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {4}}=2.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {4}}=2.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ed2dbcc9e0516408006fdc997dc259daedfe4781" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:12.434ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This  formula is valid only if the eight values with which we began form the complete population. If the values instead were a random sample drawn from some large parent population (for example, they were 8 marks randomly and independently chosen from a class of 2&#160;million), then one often divides by <span class="nowrap">7&#160;(which is <i>n</i> &#8722; 1)</span> instead of <span class="nowrap">8&#160;(which is <i>n</i>)</span> in the denominator of the last formula. In that case the result of the original formula would be called the <i>sample</i> standard deviation. Dividing by <i>n</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1 rather than by <i>n</i> gives an unbiased estimate of the variance of the larger parent population. This is known as <i><a href="/wiki/Bessel%27s_correction" title="Bessel\'s correction">Bessel\'s correction</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_deviation_of_average_height_for_adult_men">Standard deviation of average height for adult men</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Standard deviation of average height for adult men">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If the population of interest is approximately normally distributed, the standard deviation provides information on the proportion of observations above or below certain values. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Average_human_height" title="Average human height">average height for adult men</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> is about 70&#160;inches (177.8&#160;cm), with a standard deviation of around 3&#160;inches (7.62&#160;cm). This means that most men (about 68%, assuming a <a href="/wiki/Normal_distribution" title="Normal distribution">normal distribution</a>) have a height within 3&#160;inches (7.62&#160;cm) of the mean (67&#8211;73&#160;inches (170.18&#8211;185.42&#160;cm))&#160;&#8211; one standard deviation&#160;&#8211; and almost all men (about 95%) have a height within 6&#160;inches (15.24&#160;cm) of the mean (64&#8211;76&#160;inches (162.56&#8211;193.04&#160;cm))&#160;&#8211; two standard deviations. If the standard deviation were zero, then all men would be exactly 70&#160;inches (177.8&#160;cm) tall. If the standard deviation were 20&#160;inches (50.8&#160;cm), then men would have much more variable heights, with a typical range of about 50&#8211;90&#160;inches (127&#8211;228.6&#160;cm). Three standard deviations account for 99.7% of the sample population being studied, assuming the distribution is <a href="/wiki/Normal_distribution" title="Normal distribution">normal</a> (bell-shaped). (See the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/68-95-99.7_rule" title="68-95-99.7 rule">68-95-99.7 rule</a>, or the <i>empirical rule,</i> for more information.)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_of_population_values">Definition of population values</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Definition of population values">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Let <i>X</i> be a <a href="/wiki/Random_variable" title="Random variable">random variable</a> with mean value <i>&#956;</i>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\operatorname {E} [X]=\\mu .\\,\\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mo>.</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\operatorname {E} [X]=\\mu .\\,\\!}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\operatorname {E} [X]=\\mu .\\,\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a850f6d56e315eaef8b630976d5164b368ecb072" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:10.391ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Here the operator E denotes the average or <a href="/wiki/Expected_value" title="Expected value">expected value</a> of <i>X</i>.  Then the <b>standard deviation</b> of <i>X</i> is the quantity\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}\\sigma &amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [(X-\\mu )^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]+\\operatorname {E} [-2\\mu X]+\\operatorname {E} [\\mu ^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu \\operatorname {E} [X]+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu ^{2}+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-(\\operatorname {E} [X])^{2}}}\\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt">\n<mtr>\n<mtd>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">E</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mtd>\n</mtr>\n</mtable>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}\\sigma &amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [(X-\\mu )^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]+\\operatorname {E} [-2\\mu X]+\\operatorname {E} [\\mu ^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu \\operatorname {E} [X]+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu ^{2}+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-(\\operatorname {E} [X])^{2}}}\\end{aligned}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}\\sigma &amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [(X-\\mu )^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]+\\operatorname {E} [-2\\mu X]+\\operatorname {E} [\\mu ^{2}]}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu \\operatorname {E} [X]+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-2\\mu ^{2}+\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-\\mu ^{2}}}\\\\&amp;={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {E} [X^{2}]-(\\operatorname {E} [X])^{2}}}\\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5989cb6c9ab3f8a7b49459edbdad1b01dbbce57e" style="vertical-align: -14.338ex; width:33.673ex; height:29.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>(derived using the <a href="/wiki/Expected_value#Properties" title="Expected value">properties of expected value</a>).\n</p><p>In other words, the standard deviation <i>&#963;</i> (<a href="/wiki/Sigma" title="Sigma">sigma</a>) is the square root of the <a href="/wiki/Variance" title="Variance">variance</a> of <i>X</i>; i.e., it is the square root of the average value of (<i>X</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;<i>&#956;</i>)<sup>2</sup>.\n</p><p>The standard deviation of a (<a href="/wiki/Univariate" title="Univariate">univariate</a>) probability distribution is the same as that of a random variable having that distribution.  Not all random variables have a standard deviation, since these expected values need not exist. For example, the standard deviation of a random variable that follows a <a href="/wiki/Cauchy_distribution" title="Cauchy distribution">Cauchy distribution</a> is undefined because its expected value <i>&#956;</i> is undefined.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrete_random_variable">Discrete random variable</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Discrete random variable">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the case where <i>X</i> takes random values from a finite data set <i>x</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>2</sub>, ..., <i>x<sub>N</sub></i>, with each value having the same probability, the standard deviation is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\left[(x_{1}-\\mu )^{2}+(x_{2}-\\mu )^{2}+\\cdots +(x_{N}-\\mu )^{2}\\right]}},{\\rm {\\ \\ where\\ \\ }}\\mu ={\\frac {1}{N}}(x_{1}+\\cdots +x_{N}),}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mo>&#8943;<!-- &#8943; --></mo>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n<mo>]</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">w</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">h</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; In this case, the standard deviation will be\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {\\sum _{i=1}^{N}p_{i}(x_{i}-\\mu )^{2}}},{\\rm {\\ \\ where\\ \\ }}\\mu =\\sum _{i=1}^{N}p_{i}x_{i}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; width:44.119ex; height:8.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continuous_random_variable">Continuous random variable</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Continuous random variable">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The standard deviation of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continuous_distribution" title="Continuous distribution">continuous real-valued random variable</a> <i>X</i> with <a href="/wiki/Probability_density_function" title="Probability density function">probability density function</a> <i>p</i>(<i>x</i>) is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }(x-\\mu )^{2}\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x}},{\\rm {\\ \\ where\\ \\ }}\\mu =\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }x\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963;
