--></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mo>&#8747;<!-- &#8747; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="bold">X</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }(x-\\mu )^{2}\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x}},{\\rm {\\ \\ where\\ \\ }}\\mu =\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }x\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma ={\\sqrt {\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }(x-\\mu )^{2}\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x}},{\\rm {\\ \\ where\\ \\ }}\\mu =\\int _{\\mathbf {X} }x\\,p(x)\\,{\\rm {d}}x,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5a0e3e2724af7c91cea2d6a7a2fc0d17be086d78" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:52.67ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>and where the integrals are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definite_integral" title="Definite integral">definite integrals</a> taken for <i>x</i> ranging over the set of possible values of the random variable&#160;<i>X</i>.\n</p><p>In the case of a <a href="/wiki/Parametric_model" title="Parametric model">parametric family of distributions</a>, the standard deviation can be expressed in terms of the parameters.  For example, in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Log-normal_distribution" title="Log-normal distribution">log-normal distribution</a> with parameters <i>&#956;</i> and <i>&#963;</i><sup>2</sup>, the standard deviation is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {(e^{\\sigma ^{2}}-1)e^{2\\mu +\\sigma ^{2}}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {(e^{\\sigma ^{2}}-1)e^{2\\mu +\\sigma ^{2}}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {(e^{\\sigma ^{2}}-1)e^{2\\mu +\\sigma ^{2}}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d0cac8694d31a77588f1f68affb53017ddad35ce" style="vertical-align: -1.505ex; width:18.051ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Estimation">Estimation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Estimation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><span id="Estimation"></span><span id="Sample_standard_deviation"></span>\n</p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_variance" title="Sample variance">Sample variance</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unbiased_estimation_of_standard_deviation" title="Unbiased estimation of standard deviation">Unbiased estimation of standard deviation</a></div>\n<p>One can find the standard deviation of an entire population in cases (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standardized_testing_(statistics)" title="Standardized testing (statistics)">standardized testing</a>) where every member of a population is sampled. In cases where that cannot be done, the standard deviation <i>&#963;</i> is estimated by examining a random sample taken from the population and computing a <a href="/wiki/Statistic" title="Statistic">statistic</a> of the sample, which is used as an estimate of the population standard deviation. Such a statistic is called an <a href="/wiki/Estimator" title="Estimator">estimator</a>, and the estimator (or the value of the estimator, namely the estimate) is called a <b>sample standard deviation,</b> and is denoted by <i>s</i> (possibly with modifiers). However, unlike in the case of estimating the population mean, for which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_mean" title="Sample mean">sample mean</a> is a simple estimator with many desirable properties (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unbiased_estimator" title="Unbiased estimator">unbiased</a>, <a href="/wiki/Efficient_estimator" title="Efficient estimator">efficient</a>, maximum likelihood), there is no single estimator for the standard deviation with all these properties, and <a href="/wiki/Unbiased_estimation_of_standard_deviation" title="Unbiased estimation of standard deviation">unbiased estimation of standard deviation</a> is a very technically involved problem. Most often, the standard deviation is estimated using the <i><a href="#Corrected_sample_standard_deviation">corrected sample standard deviation</a></i> (using <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1), defined below, and this is often referred to as the "sample standard deviation", without qualifiers. However, other estimators are better in other respects: the uncorrected estimator (using <i>N</i>) yields lower mean squared error, while using <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1.5 (for the normal distribution) almost completely eliminates bias.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncorrected_sample_standard_deviation">Uncorrected sample standard deviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Uncorrected sample standard deviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The formula for the <i>population</i> standard deviation (of a finite population) can be applied to the sample, using the size of the sample as the size of the population (though the actual population size from which the sample is drawn may be much larger). This estimator, denoted by <i>s</i><sub><i>N</i></sub>, is known as the <b>uncorrected sample standard deviation</b>, or sometimes the <b>standard deviation of the sample</b> (considered as the entire population), and is defined as follows:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bad80ea0e24daf81761136ee19f8e46b7c7a7628" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:24.786ex; height:8.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mo>&#8230;<!-- &#8230; --></mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\{x_{1},\\,x_{2},\\,\\ldots ,\\,x_{N}\\}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c14e1c22ce19d99df6409a800191a33818ad3229" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.487ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> are the observed values of the sample items and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle {\\bar {x}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3199cb53071b8a4c7d5652988e10b5135e2fb638" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the mean value of these observations, while the denominator&#160;<i>N</i> stands for the size of the sample: this is the square root of the sample variance, which is the average of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squared_deviations" title="Squared deviations">squared deviations</a> about the sample mean.\n</p><p>This is a <a href="/wiki/Consistent_estimator" title="Consistent estimator">consistent estimator</a> (it converges in probability to the population value as the number of samples goes to infinity), and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maximum_likelihood" title="Maximum likelihood">maximum-likelihood estimate</a> when the population is normally distributed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, this is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biased_estimator" title="Biased estimator">biased estimator</a>, as the estimates are generally too low. The bias decreases as sample size grows, dropping off as 1/<i>N</i>, and thus is most significant for small or moderate sample sizes; for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle N&gt;75}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&gt;</mo>\n<mn>75</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle N&gt;75}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle N&gt;75}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/25a18d91e333a7d52cbc524127039ba831f08895" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.487ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> the bias is below 1%. Thus for very large sample sizes, the uncorrected sample standard deviation is generally acceptable. This estimator also has a uniformly smaller <a href="/wiki/Mean_squared_error" title="Mean squared error">mean squared error</a> than the corrected sample standard deviation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corrected_sample_standard_deviation">Corrected sample standard deviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Corrected sample standard deviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If the <i>biased <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_variance" title="Sample variance">sample variance</a></i> (the second <a href="/wiki/Central_moment" title="Central moment">central moment</a> of the sample, which is a downward-biased estimate of the population variance) is used to compute an estimate of the population\'s standard deviation, the result is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="s_{N}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3f51f21e26a7f7288eeb39fc640c97d2abf127c0" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:24.901ex; height:8.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Here taking the square root introduces further downward bias, by <a href="/wiki/Jensen%27s_inequality" title="Jensen\'s inequality">Jensen\'s inequality</a>, due to the square root being a <a href="/wiki/Concave_function" title="Concave function">concave function</a>. The bias in the variance is easily corrected, but the bias from the square root is more difficult to correct, and depends on the distribution in question.\n</p><p>An unbiased estimator for the <i>variance</i> is given by applying <a href="/wiki/Bessel%27s_correction" title="Bessel\'s correction">Bessel\'s correction</a>, using <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1 instead of <i>N</i> to yield the <i>unbiased sample variance,</i> denoted <i>s</i><sup>2</sup>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s^{2}={\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s^{2}={\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="s^{2}={\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a59b47025bd8e26a95e7eb0a9b5051353a200f16" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:25.813ex; height:7.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This estimator is unbiased if the variance exists and the sample values are drawn independently with replacement. <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1 corresponds to the number of <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_freedom_(statistics)" title="Degrees of freedom (statistics)">degrees of freedom</a> in the vector of deviations from the mean, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle (x_{1}-{\\overline {x}},\\;\\dots ,\\;x_{n}-{\\overline {x}}).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>\n<mo>&#8230;<!-- &#8230; --></mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>n</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle (x_{1}-{\\overline {x}},\\;\\dots ,\\;x_{n}-{\\overline {x}}).}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle (x_{1}-{\\overline {x}},\\;\\dots ,\\;x_{n}-{\\overline {x}}).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4df8ab4a29f607810872ee7175cdc0168d7e8251" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:22.427ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>\n</p><p>Taking square roots reintroduces bias (because the square root is a nonlinear function, which does not <a href="/wiki/Commutative_property" title="Commutative property">commute</a> with the expectation), yielding the <b>corrected sample standard deviation,</b> denoted by <i>s:</i>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle s={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="s={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1bffdcb1ecd0b326bb7ad67397b073af9c15fa6e" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:27.212ex; height:8.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>As explained above, while <i>s</i><sup>2</sup> is an unbiased estimator for the population variance, <i>s</i> is still a biased estimator for the population standard deviation, though markedly less biased than the uncorrected sample standard deviation. This estimator is commonly used and generally known simply as the "sample standard deviation". The bias may still be large for small samples (<i>N</i> less than 10). As sample size increases, the amount of bias decreases. We obtain more information and the difference between <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{N}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{N}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\frac  {1}{N}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8fb12c5f73f8763997550a9abdf59b00c4932ee4" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:2.9ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{N-1}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{N-1}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {1}{N-1}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a7e023c572c9945fa519bcbaaba4ff79c1a1fe2e" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:6.903ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span> becomes smaller.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unbiased_sample_standard_deviation">Unbiased sample standard deviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Unbiased sample standard deviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For <a href="/wiki/Unbiased_estimation_of_standard_deviation" title="Unbiased estimation of standard deviation">unbiased estimation of standard deviation</a>, there is no formula that works across all distributions, unlike for mean and variance. Instead, <i>s</i> is used as a basis, and is scaled by a correction factor to produce an unbiased estimate. For the normal distribution, an unbiased estimator is given by <i>s</i>/<i>c</i><sub>4</sub>, where the correction factor (which depends on <i>N</i>) is given in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Gamma_function" title="Gamma function">Gamma function</a>, and equals:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle c_{4}(N)\\,=\\,{\\sqrt {\\frac {2}{N-1}}}\\,\\,\\,{\\frac {\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N}{2}}\\right)}{\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N-1}{2}}\\right)}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>4</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#915;<!-- &#915; --></mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#915;<!-- &#915; --></mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c_{4}(N)\\,=\\,{\\sqrt {\\frac {2}{N-1}}}\\,\\,\\,{\\frac {\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N}{2}}\\right)}{\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N-1}{2}}\\right)}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="c_{4}(N)\\,=\\,{\\sqrt {\\frac {2}{N-1}}}\\,\\,\\,{\\frac {\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N}{2}}\\right)}{\\Gamma \\left({\\frac {N-1}{2}}\\right)}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/25613f32c2e1c44c5c82dd8fc60f3e27ec2931b0" style="vertical-align: -4.505ex; width:30.689ex; height:10.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This arises because the sampling distribution of the sample standard deviation follows a (scaled) <a href="/wiki/Chi_distribution" title="Chi distribution">chi distribution</a>, and the correction factor is the mean of the chi distribution.\n</p><p>An approximation can be given by replacing <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1 with <i>N</i>&#160;&#8722;&#160;1.5, yielding:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1.5</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1fa4305ff136ea2fadc32e6156dc7f510dd1a0ca" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:29.146ex; height:8.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The error in this approximation decays quadratically (as 1/<i>N</i><sup>2</sup>), and it is suited for all but the smallest samples or highest precision: for <i>N</i> = 3 the bias is equal to 1.3%, and for <i>N</i> = 9 the bias is already less than 0.1%.\nA more accurate approximation is to replace <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle N-1.5}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1.5</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle N-1.5}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle N-1.5}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fd8aa960232df9f20d40f90a4dc5bd253f8dc646" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:7.876ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> above with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle N-1.5+1/(8(N-1))}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1.5</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>8</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle N-1.5+1/(8(N-1))}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle N-1.5+1/(8(N-1))}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ea08076fdc0e36cefde70d22bd643605e4f54903" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:23.889ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>.\n</p><p>For other distributions, the correct formula depends on the distribution, but a rule of thumb is to use the further refinement of the approximation:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5-{\\tfrac {1}{4}}\\gamma _{2}}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>1.5</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mn>4</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#947;<!-- &#947; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<munderover>\n<mo>&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munderover>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5-{\\tfrac {1}{4}}\\gamma _{2}}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\sigma }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N-1.5-{\\tfrac {1}{4}}\\gamma _{2}}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\bar {x}})^{2}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d88acfa567ea5f091c6d577b74eedbed96ce0842" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:35.903ex; height:8.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>&#947;</i><sub>2</sub> denotes the population <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excess_kurtosis" title="Excess kurtosis">excess kurtosis</a>. The excess kurtosis may be either known beforehand for certain distributions, or estimated from the data.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Confidence_interval_of_a_sampled_standard_deviation">Confidence interval of a sampled standard deviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Confidence interval of a sampled standard deviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Margin_of_error" title="Margin of error">Margin of error</a>, <a href="/wiki/Variance#Distribution_of_the_sample_variance" title="Variance">Variance &#167;&#160;Distribution of the sample variance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Student%27s_t-distribution#Robust_parametric_modeling" title="Student\'s t-distribution">Student\'s_t-distribution &#167;&#160;Robust_parametric_modeling</a></div>\n<p>The standard deviation we obtain by sampling a distribution is itself not absolutely accurate, both for mathematical reasons (explained here by the confidence interval) and for practical reasons of measurement (measurement error). The mathematical effect can be described by the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval" title="Confidence interval">confidence interval</a> or CI. \nTo show how a larger sample will make the confidence interval narrower, consider the following examples: \nA small population of <i>N</i> = 2 has only 1 degree of freedom for estimating the standard deviation.  The result is that a 95% CI of the SD runs from 0.45&#160;&#215;&#160;SD to 31.9&#160;&#215;&#160;SD;  <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval#Statistical_theory" title="Confidence interval">the factors here are as follows</a>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{\\sigma ^{2}}}&lt;q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">Pr</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<mi>k</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{\\sigma ^{2}}}&lt;q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha ,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{\\sigma ^{2}}}&lt;q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha ,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2864b1edfdf24d32158185036a19d14a1bd34a20" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:34.187ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q_{p}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q_{p}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle q_{p}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2a1a924af25b278a955bfab1e1b0a437aa3389a9" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.096ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is the <i>p</i>-th quantile of the chi-square distribution with <i>k</i> degrees of freedom, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 1-\\alpha }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 1-\\alpha }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="1-\\alpha" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9afa7876fb8b4fb8c4d8039ebed6cd1cbc4781cd" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:5.49ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is the confidence level.  This is equivalent to the following:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}}&lt;\\sigma ^{2}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">Pr</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mi>k</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<mi>k</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>s</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}}&lt;\\sigma ^{2}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha .}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Pr \\left(k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{1-{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}}&lt;\\sigma ^{2}&lt;k{\\frac {s^{2}}{q_{\\frac {\\alpha }{2}}}}\\right)=1-\\alpha .}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a09ce9cc225389bdf3f81ec57d8f76a269d84731" style="vertical-align: -3.505ex; width:36.494ex; height:7.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>With <i>k</i> = 1, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q_{0.025}=0.000982}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0.025</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0.000982</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q_{0.025}=0.000982}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle q_{0.025}=0.000982}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c2ed16579b63960abf234afca809639056f36d05" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.897ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle q_{0.975}=5.024}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>q</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0.975</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>5.024</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle q_{0.975}=5.024}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle q_{0.975}=5.024}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cefb0a081d6f851aa7c1ea0ab0f92cd3a70827a7" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.41ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>.  The reciprocals of the square roots of these two numbers give us the factors 0.45 and 31.9 given above.\n</p><p>A larger population of <i>N</i> = 10 has 9 degrees of freedom for estimating the standard deviation.  The same computations as above give us in this case a 95% CI running from 0.69&#160;&#215;&#160;SD to 1.83&#160;&#215;&#160;SD. So even with a sample population of 10, the actual SD can still be almost a factor 2 higher than the sampled SD. For a sample population N=100, this is down to 0.88&#160;&#215;&#160;SD to 1.16&#160;&#215;&#160;SD. To be more certain that the sampled SD is close to the actual SD we need to sample a large number of points.\n</p><p>These same formulae can be used to obtain confidence intervals on the variance of residuals from a <a href="/wiki/Least_squares" title="Least squares">least squares</a> fit under standard normal theory, where <i>k</i> is now the number of <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_freedom_(statistics)" title="Degrees of freedom (statistics)">degrees of freedom</a> for error.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Identities_and_mathematical_properties">Identities and mathematical properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Identities and mathematical properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The standard deviation is invariant under changes in <a href="/wiki/Location_parameter" title="Location parameter">location</a>, and scales directly with the <a href="/wiki/Scale_parameter" title="Scale parameter">scale</a> of the random variable. Thus, for a constant <i>c</i> and random variables <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma (c)=0\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma (c)=0\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\sigma (c)=0\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0380ce3739381e7eb4015293711d2b9871ce8ace" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:8.794ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma (X+c)=\\sigma (X),\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma (X+c)=\\sigma (X),\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\sigma (X+c)=\\sigma (X),\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc00f52f6ad0a565746867004d2d84d71b401ea5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.218ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma (cX)=|c|\\sigma (X).\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>.</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma (cX)=|c|\\sigma (X).\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\sigma (cX)=|c|\\sigma (X).\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c611b9ef1d2ea3021b7c5b4ee8c6450ee188edac" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.678ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The standard deviation of the sum of two random variables can be related to their individual standard deviations and the <a href="/wiki/Covariance" title="Covariance">covariance</a> between them:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma (X+Y)={\\sqrt {\\operatorname {var} (X)+\\operatorname {var} (Y)+2\\,\\operatorname {cov} (X,Y)}}.\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>Y</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mi>var</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>X</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>var</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; width:9.559ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {cov} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>cov</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {cov} }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {cov} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9c0b3d989899b33809286b4e87bd33c2da0b7cd3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; In the following formula, the letter E is interpreted to mean expected value, i.e., mean.\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\left(\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}^{2}\\right)-({\\overline {x}})^{2}}}={\\sqrt {\\left({\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}^{2}\\right)-\\left({\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}\\right)^{2}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {1}{N}}\\left(\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}^{2}\\right)-({\\overline {x}})^{2}}}={\\sqrt {\\left({\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}^{2}\\right)-\\left({\\frac {1}{N}}\\sum _{i=1}^{N}x_{i}\\right)^{2}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2997341589a4efdd516438ba39d5def1293f79a7" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:80.196ex; height:8.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This means that the standard deviation is equal to the square root of the difference between the average of the squares of the values and the square of the average value.\nSee <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computational_formula_for_the_variance" title="Computational formula for the variance">computational formula for the variance</a> for proof, and for an analogous result for the sample standard deviation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interpretation_and_application">Interpretation and application</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Interpretation and application">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Prediction_interval" title="Prediction interval">Prediction interval</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confidence_interval" title="Confidence interval">Confidence interval</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comparison_standard_deviations.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="296" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Comparison_standard_deviations.svg/400px-Comparison_standard_deviations.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Comparison_standard_deviations.svg/600px-Comparison_standard_deviations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Comparison_standard_deviations.svg/800px-Comparison_standard_deviations.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Comparison_standard_deviations.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example of samples from two populations with the same mean but different standard deviations. Red population has mean 100 and SD 10; blue population has mean 100 and SD 50.</div></div></div>\n<p>A large standard deviation indicates that the data points can spread far from the mean and a small standard deviation indicates that they are clustered closely around the mean.\n</p><p>For example, each of the three populations {0, 0, 14, 14}, {0, 6, 8, 14} and {6, 6, 8, 8} has a mean of 7. Their standard deviations are 7, 5, and 1, respectively. The third population has a much smaller standard deviation than the other two because its values are all close to 7. It will have the same units as the data points themselves. If, for instance, the data set {0, 6, 8, 14} represents the ages of a population of four siblings in years, the standard deviation is 5 years. As another example, the population {1000, 1006, 1008, 1014} may represent the distances traveled by four athletes, measured in meters. It has a mean of 1007 meters, and a standard deviation of 5 meters.\n</p><p>Standard deviation may serve as a measure of uncertainty.  In physical science, for example, the reported standard deviation of a group of repeated <a href="/wiki/Measurement" title="Measurement">measurements</a> gives the <a href="/wiki/Accuracy_and_precision" title="Accuracy and precision">precision</a> of those measurements.  When deciding whether measurements agree with a theoretical prediction, the standard deviation of those measurements is of crucial importance:  if the mean of the measurements is too far away from the prediction (with the distance measured in standard deviations), then the theory being tested probably needs to be revised. This makes sense since they fall outside the range of values that could reasonably be expected to occur, if the prediction were correct and the standard deviation appropriately quantified.  See <a href="/wiki/Prediction_interval" title="Prediction interval">prediction interval</a>.\n</p><p>While the standard deviation does measure how far typical values tend to be from the mean, other measures are available. An example is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mean_absolute_deviation" title="Mean absolute deviation">mean absolute deviation</a>, which might be considered a more direct measure of average distance, compared to the <a href="/wiki/Root-mean-square_deviation" title="Root-mean-square deviation">root mean square distance</a> inherent in the standard deviation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Application_examples">Application examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Application examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The practical value of understanding the standard deviation of a set of values is in appreciating how much variation there is from the average (mean).\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Experiment.2C_industrial_and_hypothesis_testing"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Experiment,_industrial_and_hypothesis_testing">Experiment, industrial and hypothesis testing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Experiment, industrial and hypothesis testing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Standard deviation is often used to compare real-world data against a model to test the model.\nFor example, in industrial applications the weight of products coming off a production line may need to comply with a legally required value. By weighing some fraction of the products an average weight can be found, which will always be slightly different to the long-term average. By using standard deviations, a minimum and maximum value can be calculated that the averaged weight will be within some very high percentage of the time (99.9% or more). If it falls outside the range then the production process may need to be corrected. Statistical tests such as these are particularly important when the testing is relatively expensive. For example, if the product needs to be opened and drained and weighed, or if the product was otherwise used up by the test.\n</p><p>In experimental science, a theoretical model of reality is used. <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">Particle physics</a> conventionally uses a standard of "5 sigma" for the declaration of a discovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> A five-sigma level translates to one chance in 3.5 million that a random fluctuation would yield the result. This level of certainty was required in order to assert that a particle consistent with the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a> had been discovered in two independent experiments at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and this was also the significance level leading to the declaration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GW150914" title="GW150914">first detection of gravitational waves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">Weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Weather">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As a simple example, consider the average daily maximum temperatures for two cities, one inland and one on the coast. It is helpful to understand that the range of daily maximum temperatures for cities near the coast is smaller than for cities inland. Thus, while these two cities may each have the same average maximum temperature, the standard deviation of the daily maximum temperature for the coastal city will be less than that of the inland city as, on any particular day, the actual maximum temperature is more likely to be farther from the average maximum temperature for the inland city than for the coastal one.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In finance, standard deviation is often used as a measure of the <a href="/wiki/Risk#Finance" title="Risk">risk</a> associated with price-fluctuations of a given asset (stocks, bonds, property, etc.), or the risk of a portfolio of assets<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> (actively managed mutual funds, index mutual funds, or ETFs). Risk is an important factor in determining how to efficiently manage a portfolio of investments because it determines the variation in returns on the asset and/or portfolio and gives investors a mathematical basis for investment decisions (known as <a href="/wiki/Modern_portfolio_theory" title="Modern portfolio theory">mean-variance optimization</a>). The fundamental concept of risk is that as it increases, the expected return on an investment should increase as well, an increase known as the risk premium. In other words, investors should expect a higher return on an investment when that investment carries a higher level of risk or uncertainty. When evaluating investments, investors should estimate both the expected return and the uncertainty of future returns. Standard deviation provides a quantified estimate of the uncertainty of future returns.\n</p><p>For example, assume an investor had to choose between two stocks. Stock A over the past 20 years had an average return of 10 percent, with a standard deviation of 20 <a href="/wiki/Percentage_point" title="Percentage point">percentage points</a> (pp) and Stock B, over the same period, had average returns of 12 percent but a higher standard deviation of 30 pp. On the basis of risk and return, an investor may decide that Stock A is the safer choice, because Stock B\'s additional two percentage points of return is not worth the additional 10 pp standard deviation (greater risk or uncertainty of the expected return). Stock B is likely to fall short of the initial investment (but also to exceed the initial investment) more often than Stock A under the same circumstances, and is estimated to return only two percent more on average. In this example, Stock A is expected to earn about 10 percent, plus or minus 20 pp (a range of 30 percent to &#8722;10 percent), about two-thirds of the future year returns. When considering more extreme possible returns or outcomes in future, an investor should expect results of as much as 10 percent plus or minus 60 pp, or a range from 70 percent to &#8722;50 percent, which includes outcomes for three standard deviations from the average return (about 99.7 percent of probable returns).\n</p><p>Calculating the average (or arithmetic mean) of the return of a security over a given period will generate the expected return of the asset. For each period, subtracting the expected return from the actual return results in the difference from the mean.  Squaring the difference in each period and taking the average gives the overall variance of the return of the asset.  The larger the variance, the greater risk the security carries.  Finding the square root of this variance will give the standard deviation of the investment tool in question.\n</p><p>Population standard deviation is used to set the width of <a href="/wiki/Bollinger_Bands" title="Bollinger Bands">Bollinger Bands</a>, a widely adopted <a href="/wiki/Technical_analysis" title="Technical analysis">technical analysis</a> tool. For example, the upper Bollinger Band is given as <span class="nowrap"><span style="text-decoration:overline;"><i>x</i></span> + <i>n&#963;<sub>x</sub></i>.</span> The most commonly used value for <i>n</i> is 2; there is about a five percent chance of going outside, assuming a normal distribution of returns.\n</p><p>Financial time series are known to be non-stationary series, whereas the statistical calculations above, such as standard deviation, apply only to stationary series. To apply the above statistical tools to non-stationary series, the series first must be transformed to a stationary series, enabling use of statistical tools that now have a valid basis from which to work.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geometric_interpretation">Geometric interpretation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Geometric interpretation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>To gain some geometric insights and clarification, we will start with a population of three values, <i>x</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>2</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>3</sub>. This defines a point <i>P</i> = (<i>x</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>2</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>3</sub>) in <b>R</b><sup>3</sup>. Consider the line <i>L</i> = {(<i>r</i>, <i>r</i>, <i>r</i>)&#160;: <i>r</i> &#8712; <b>R</b>}. This is the "main diagonal" going through the origin. If our three given values were all equal, then the standard deviation would be zero and <i>P</i> would lie on <i>L</i>. So it is not unreasonable to assume that the standard deviation is related to the <i>distance</i> of <i>P</i> to <i>L</i>. That is indeed the case. To move orthogonally from <i>L</i> to the point <i>P</i>, one begins at the point:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle M=({\\overline {x}},{\\overline {x}},{\\overline {x}})}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>M</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; width:13.752ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>whose coordinates are the mean of the values we started out with. \n</p>\n<div style="margin-left:0">\n<table class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="background: transparent; width:36.174ex; height:37.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>A little algebra shows that the distance between <i>P</i> and <i>M</i> (which is the same as the orthogonal distance between <i>P</i> and the line <i>L</i>) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {\\sum \\limits _{i}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<munder>\n<mo movablelimits="false">&#8721;<!-- &#8721; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</munder>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {\\sum \\limits _{i}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\sqrt {\\sum \\limits _{i}(x_{i}-{\\overline {x}})^{2}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b71a98ba60f18ced4880b365fb56f1adac269e79" style="vertical-align: -3.338ex; width:14.957ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span> is equal to the standard deviation of the vector (<i>x</i><sub>1</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>2</sub>, <i>x</i><sub>3</sub>), multiplied by the square root of the number of dimensions of the vector (3 in this case).\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Chebyshev.27s_inequality"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chebyshev\'s_inequality">Chebyshev\'s inequality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chebyshev\'s inequality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chebyshev%27s_inequality" title="Chebyshev\'s inequality">Chebyshev\'s inequality</a></div>\n<p>An observation is rarely more than a few standard deviations away from the mean. Chebyshev\'s inequality ensures that, for all distributions for which the standard deviation is defined, the amount of data within a number of standard deviations of the mean is at least as much as given in the following table.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Distance from mean</th>\n<th>Minimum population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\sqrt {2}}\\,\\sigma }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; width:0.97ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rules_for_normally_distributed_data">Rules for normally distributed data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Standard_deviation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rules for normally distributed data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Standard_deviation_diagram.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/220px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/330px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Standard_deviation_diagram.svg/440px-Standard_deviation_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Standard_deviation_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dark blue is one standard deviation on either side of the mean. For the normal distribution, this accounts for 68.27 percent of the set; while two standard deviations from the mean (medium and dark blue) account for 95.45 percent; three standard deviations (light, medium, and dark blue) account for 99.73 percent; and four standard deviations account for 99.994 percent. The two points of the curve that are one standard deviation from the mean are also the <a href="/wiki/Inflection_point" title="Inflection point">inflection points</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_limit_theorem" title="Central limit theorem">central limit theorem</a> states that the distribution of an average of many independent, identically distributed random variables tends toward the famous bell-shaped normal distribution with a <a href="/wiki/Probability_density_function" title="Probability density function">probability density function</a> of\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle f(x;\\mu ,\\sigma ^{2})={\\frac {1}{\\sigma {\\sqrt {2\\pi }}}}e^{-{\\frac {1}{2}}\\left({\\frac {x-\\mu }{\\sigma }}\\right)^{2}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>f</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>;</mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle f(x;\\mu ,\\sigma ^{2})={\\frac {1}{\\sigma {\\sqrt {2\\pi }}}}e^{-{\\frac {1}{2}}\\left({\\frac {x-\\mu }{\\sigma }}\\right)^{2}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="f(x;\\mu ,\\sigma ^{2})={\\frac {1}{\\sigma {\\sqrt {2\\pi }}}}e^{-{\\frac {1}{2}}\\left({\\frac {x-\\mu }{\\sigma }}\\right)^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a9e66f831f31efc53adc1663d3fc80f0f6307061" style="vertical-align: -2.838ex; width:30.301ex; height:6.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>&#956;</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Expected_value" title="Expected value">expected value</a> of the random variables, <i>&#963;</i> equals their distribution\'s standard deviation divided by <i>n</i><sup>1/2</sup>, and <i>n</i> is the number of random variables.  The standard deviation therefore is simply a scaling variable that adjusts how broad the curve will be, though it also appears in the <a href="/wiki/Normalizing_constant" title="Normalizing constant">normalizing constant</a>.\n</p><p>If a data distribution is approximately normal, then the proportion of data values within <i>z</i> standard deviations of the mean is defined by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\text{Proportion}}=\\operatorname {erf} \\left({\\frac {z}{\\sqrt {2}}}\\right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>Proportion</mtext>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>erf</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>z</mi>\n<msqrt>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</msqrt>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\text{Proportion}}=\\operatorname {erf} \\left({\\frac {z}{\\sqrt {2}}}\\right)}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle {\\text{Proportion}}=\\operatorname {erf} \\left({\\frac {z}{\\sqrt {2}}}\\right)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f147e9e44560be306bf3c3c09f75790b9cc795f" style="vertical-align: -2.838ex; width:24.14ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {erf} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>erf</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {erf} }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\textstyle \\operatorname {erf} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/236a5d4cc1c03991644e45560c49533eda66bdd3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-right: -0.153ex; width:2.809ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Error_function" title="Error function">error function</a>. The proportion that is less than or equal to a number, <i>x</i>, is given by the <a href="/wiki/Cumulative_distribution_function" title="Cumulative distribution function">cumulative distribution function</a>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\text{Proportion}}\\leq x={\\frac {1}{2}}\\left[1+\\operatorname {erf} \\left({\\frac {x-\\mu }{\\sigma {\\sqrt {2}}}}\\right)\\right]={\\frac {1}{2}}\\left[1+\\operatorname {erf} \\left({\\frac {z}{\\sqrt {2}}}\\right)\\right]}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>Proportion</mtext>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8804;<!-- &#8804; --></mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mo>[</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>erf</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289;
